		- 11.1
			- Zenme ban↔what to do10. 预报 yùbào v to forecast
			- 天气↔tianqì n weather
			- 比↔bǐ to compare; (followed by a noun and adjective) more {adj.} than {noun}; ratio; to gesture; (Taiwan pr. [bi4] in some compounds derived from Classical Chinese); Belgium; Belgian; abbr. for 比利时
			- 下雪↔xià xuě vo to snow
			- 雪↔xuě "snow; snowfall; Classifiers: 场 ; to have the appearance of snow; to wipe away, off or out; to clean; surname Xue"
			- 约↔yue v to make an appointment
			- 公园↔gongyuán n park
			- 园↔yuán "land used for growing plants; site used for public recreation; abbr. for a place ending in 园 , such as a botanical garden 植物园 , kindergarten 幼儿园 etc; surname Yuan"
			- 滑冰↔huá bing vo to ice skate
			- 滑↔huá to slip; to slide; smooth; slippery; cunning; surname Hua
			- 冰↔bīng ice; Classifiers: 块 ; to chill sth; (of an object or substance) to feel cold; (of a person) cold; unfriendly; (slang) methamphetamine; variant of 冰
			- 会↔huì mv will [See Grammar 3.]
			- 刚才↔gangcái t just now; a moment ago
			- 网上↔wang shang on the internet
			- 预报↔yùbào v to forecast
			- 刚↔gāng hard; firm; strong; just; barely; exactly
			- 报↔bào to announce; to inform; report; newspaper; recompense; revenge; Classifiers: 份
			- 更↔gèng even more; further; still; still more
			- 不但…，而且…↔búdàn…, érqie… conj not only…, but also…
			- 且↔qiě and; moreover; yet; for the time being; to be about to; both (… and…)
			- 暖和↔nuanhuo adj warm
			- 暖↔nuǎn "warm; to warm; old variant of 暖 ; variant of 暖 , warm; variant of 暖"
			- 办↔bàn v to handle; to do
			- 冷↔lěng cold; surname Leng
			- 碟↔dié n disc; small plate, dish, saucer
			- Dialogue
				- Gao Xiaoyin: Today’s weather is better than yesterday’s. It’s not snowing anymore.↔Jintian tianqì bı zuótian haˇo, bú xià xue lek.
				- Gao Wenzhong: I asked a friend to go ice skating in the park tomorrow. I wonder what the weather is going to be like.↔Woˇ yue le péngyou míngtian qù gongyuán huá bing, bù zhidào tianqì huìl zenmeyàng?
				- Gao Xiaoyin: I looked up the forecast on the internet. Tomorrow’s weather will be even better than today. Not only will it not snow, it’ll be a bit warmer, too.↔Woˇ gangcái kàn le waˇng shang de tianqì yùbào, míngtian tianqì bıˇ jintian gèng haˇo. Búdàn bú huì xià xue, érqie huì nuaˇnhuo yì diaˇnrm.
				- Gao Wenzhong: Really? Fantastic!↔Shì ma? Tài haˇo le!
				- Gao Xiaoyin: Whom did you ask to go ice skating?→Nıˇ yue le shéi qù huá bing?
				- Gao Wenzhong: Bai Ying’ai.↔Bái Ying’ài.
				- Gao Xiaoyin: You asked Bai Ying’ai? But she flew to New York this morning.↔Nıˇ yue le Bái Ying’ài? Keshì ta jintian zaˇoshang zuò feiji qù Niu􀀆yue le.
				- Gao Wenzhong: Really? Then what do I do tomorrow?→Zhen de a? Nà wo míngtian zenmebàn?
				- Gao Xiaoyin: Why don’t you watch a DVD at home?→Nıˇ háishi zài jia kàn diév ba!
		- 11.2
			- Dialogue
				- (Gao Wenzhong is chatting with Bai Ying’ai online.)↔(Gao Wenzheng zai wang shang zhao Bai Ying'ai lido tianr.)
				- Gao Wenzhong: Ying’ai, New York is so much fun. How come you’re online and not out and about?→Ying'ai, Niillyue name hdowanr, ni zenme zai wang shang, mei chu qu?
				- Bai Ying’ai: The weather here is awful.↔Zher de tianqi feichang zao gao.
				- Gao Wenzhong: How come?→Zenme le?
				- Bai Ying’ai: Yesterday it poured. It rained again today.↔Zuotian xia da yu, jintian you xia yu le.
				- Gao Wenzhong: The weather here is great this weekend. You’d better come back as soon as you can.↔Zhè ge zhoumò zhèr tianqì hen hao, nı kuài yì dianr huí lai ba.
				- Bai Ying’ai: It’s going to be warmer in New York this weekend. Next week I have an interview. I can’t come back just yet.↔Zhè ge zhoumò Niuyue ye huì nuanhuo yì dianr. Wo xià ge xinqi you yí ge miànshì, hái bù néng huí qu.
				- Gao Wenzhong: I found a job in California. Go with me. It’s not cold in the winter in California, or hot in the summer. Spring and fall are even more comfortable.↔Wo zài Jiazhou zhao le yí ge gongzuò, nı ye qù ba. Jiazhou dongtian bù leng, xiàtian bu re, chuntian he qiutian geng shufu.
				- Bai Ying’ai: California is great, but I like New York more.↔Jiazhou hao shi hao, keshi wo geng xihuan Niu Yue
		- 12.1
			- 饭馆儿↔fànguǎn(r) restaurant
			- 好像↔hǎoxiàng to seem; to be like
			- 位子↔wèizi seat
			- 服务员↔fúwùyuán waiter; attendant
			- 桌子↔zhuōzi table
			- 点菜↔diǎncài to order food
			- 盘↔pán plate; dish
			- 饺子↔jiǎozi dumpling
			- 素↔sù vegetarian; made from vegetables
			- 家常↔jiācháng home-style
			- 豆腐↔dòufu tofu; bean curd
			- 放↔fàng to put; to place
			- 肉↔ròu meat
			- 碗↔wǎn bowl
			- 酸辣汤↔suānlàtāng hot and sour soup
			- 味精↔wèijīng monosodium glutamate (M.S.G.)
			- 盐↔yán salt
			- 白菜↔báicài bok choy
			- 刚↔gāng just
			- 卖完↔màiwán to be sold out
			- 青菜↔qīngcài green/leafy vegetable
			- 冰茶↔bīngchá iced tea
			- 渴↔kě thirsty
			- 些↔xiē (measure word for an indefinite amount); some
			- 够↔gòu enough
			- 饿↔è hungry
			- 上菜↔shàng cài to serve food

		- 12.2
			- 师傅↔master worker - shīfu
			- 好吃↔delicious - hǎochī
			- 糖醋鱼↔sweet and sour fish - tángcùyú
			- 甜↔sweet - tián
			- 酸↔sour - suān
			- 极↔extremely - jí
			- 红烧↔soy-braised - hóngshāo
			- 牛肉↔beef - niúròu
			- 鱼↔fish - yú
			- 凉拌↔served cold - liángbàn
			- 黄瓜↔cucumber - huánggua
			- 米饭↔cooked rice - mǐfàn
			- 忘↔to forget - wàng
			- 带↔to bring - dài
			- 饭卡↔meal card - fànkǎ
			- 错↔wrong - cuò
			- 清楚↔clear - qīngchu
			- 没关系↔doesn't matter - méi guānxi
			- 上海↔Shanghai - Shànghǎi
			- Dialogue
				- (It’s Thursday. The student cafeteria is serving Chinese food. The chef is from Shanghai.)↔今天是星期四, 学生餐厅有中国菜, 师傅是上海人。Jīntiān shì xīngqīsì, xuéshēng cāntīng yǒu Zhòngguó cài, shīfu shì Shànghǎi rén.
				- Wang Peng: Chef, what’s good for dinner today?→师傅, 请问, 今天晚饭有什么好吃的? Shīfu, qǐngwèn jīntiān wǎnfàn yǒu shénme hǎochī de?
				- Chef: We’ve got sweet and sour fish. It’s a little sweet and a little sour. It’s delicious. Why don’t you get that?→我们今天有糖醋鱼, 甜甜的, 酸酸的, 好吃极了, 你买一个吧。 Wǒmen jīntiān yǒu tángcùyú, tián tián de, suān suān de, hǎochī jí le, nǐ mǎi yí ge ba.
				- Wang Peng: Great. Do you have beef braised in soy sauce today?→好。今天有没有红烧牛肉? Hǎo. Jīntiān yǒu méiyǒu hóngshāo niúròu?
				- Chef: No, we don’t. You’ve already got fish, so there’s no need to have meat. How about a cucumber salad?→没有。你已经要鱼了, 别吃肉了。 来个凉拌黄瓜吧? Méiyǒu. Nǐ yǐjīng yào yú le, bié chī ròu le. Lái ge liángbàn huánggua ba?
				- Wang Peng: All right. Give me a bowl of rice. How much all together?→好。再来一碗米饭。一共多少钱? Hǎo. Zài lái yì wǎn mǐfàn. Yígòng duōshao qián?
				- Chef: Sweet and sour fish is $4.50, cucumber salad $1.70; one bowl of rice, 50 cents. All together $6.70.↔糖醋鱼, 四块五, 凉拌黄瓜, 一块七, 一碗米饭, 五毛钱。一共六块七。Tángcùyú, sì kuài wǔ, liángbàn huánggua yí kuài qī, yì wǎn mǐfàn, wǔ máo qián. Yígòng liù kuài qī.
				- Wang Peng: Shoot, Chef. I forgot my meal card. Here’s $10.↔师傅, 糟糕, 我忘了带饭卡了。这是十块钱。Shīfu, zāogāo, wǒ wàng le dài fànkǎ le. Zhè shì shí kuài qián.
				- Chef: $3.30 is your change↔找你三块三。 Zhǎo nǐ sān kuài sān.
				- Wang Peng: Chef, you’ve given the wrong change. You gave me one dollar extra.↔师傅, 钱你找错了, 多找了我一块钱。 Shīfu, qián nǐ zhǎo cuò le, duō zhǎo le wǒ yí kuài qián.
				- Chef: I’m sorry. I didn’t see it clearly.↔对不起, 我没有看清楚。 Duìbuqǐ, wǒ méiyǒu kàn qīngchu.
				- Wang Peng: That’s all right.↔没关系。 Méi guānxi.
				- Chef: Come again next Thursday.↔下个星期四再来。 Xià ge xīngqīsì zài lái.
				- Wang Peng: OK. Bye.↔好, 再见。 Hǎo, zàijiàn.

			- 包↔bāo to cover; to wrap; to hold; to include; to take charge of; to contract (to or for); package; wrapper; container; bag; to hold or embrace; bundle; packet; Classifiers: 个 ; surname Bao
			- 超↔chāo to exceed; to overtake; to surpass; to transcend; to pass; to cross; ultra-; super-
			- 登↔dēng to scale (a height); to ascend; to mount; to publish or record; to enter (e.g. in a register); to press down with the foot; to step or tread on; to put on (shoes or trousers) (dialect); to be gathered and taken to the threshing ground (old)
			- 牌↔pái mahjong tile; playing card; game pieces; signboard; plate; tablet; medal; Classifiers: 片
			- 哭↔kū to cry; to weep
			- 顾↔gù to look after; to take into consideration; to attend to; surname Gu
			- 叔↔shū uncle; father's younger brother; husband's younger brother; Taiwan pr. [shu2]
			- 阿↔Ā "prefix used before monosyllabic names, kinship terms etc to indicate familiarity; used in transliteration; also pr. [a4]; abbr. for Afghanistan 阿富汗"
			- 姨↔yí mother's sister; aunt
			- 迎↔yíng to welcome; to meet; to face; to forge ahead (esp. in the face of difficulties)
			- 瘦↔shòu thin; to lose weight; (of clothing) tight; (of meat) lean; (of land) unproductive
			- 爷↔yé grandpa; old gentleman
			- 奶↔nǎi mother; variant of 奶 ; breast; milk; to breastfeed; variant of 奶
			- 烤↔kǎo to roast; to bake; to broil
			- 鸭↔yā duck; Classifiers: 只 ; (slang) male prostitute

			- Dialogue
				- Chang: Are classes over, Little Bai? Where are you off to?→小白, 下课了? 上哪里去? 小白, 下课了? 上哪里去? Xiǎo Bái, xià kè le? Shàng nǎlǐ qù?

				- Bai: But I don’t know how to get there.→不知道怎么走, 不知道怎么走, bù zhīdào zěnme zǒu,
				- Bai: I heard it’s next to the sportsfield.↔听说就在运动场旁边。 听说就在运动场旁边。 tīngshuō jiù zài yùndòngchǎng pángbiān.
				- Chang: The computer center is not as far as the sports field.↔电脑中心没有运动场那么远。 电脑中心没有运动场那么远。 Diànnǎo zhōngxīn méiyǒu yùndòngchǎng nàme yuǎn.
				- Chang: You know where the schoollibrary is?→你知道学校图书馆在哪里吗? 你知道学校图书馆在哪里吗? Nǐ zhīdào xuéxiào túshūguǎn zài nǎlǐ ma?
				- Bai: Yes, I do. It’s not far from Wang Peng’s dorm.↔知道, 离王朋的宿舍不远。 知道, 离王朋的宿舍不远。 Zhīdào, lí Wáng Péng de sùshè bù yuǎn.

				- Chang:It’s between thelibrary and the studentactivity center.↔就在图书馆和学生活动中心中间。 就在图书馆和学生活动中心中间。 jiù zài túshūguǎn hé xuéshēng huódòng zhōngxīn zhōngjiān.
				- Bai: Teacher Chang, where are you headed?→常老师, 您去哪里呢? 常老师, 您去哪里呢? Cháng lǎoshī, nín qù nǎlǐ ne?
				- Chan:I’d like to get some books at the school bookstore.↔我想到学校书店去买书。 我想到学校书店去买书。 Wǒ xiǎng dào xuéxiào shūdiàn qù mǎi shū.
				- Bai:Where’s the bookstore?→书店在什么地方? 书店在什么地方? Shūdiàn zài shénme dìfang?
				- Chang: It’s in the student activity center.↔就在学生活动中心里边。 就在学生活动中心里边。 Jiù zài xuéshēng huódòng zhōngxīn lǐbian.
				- Chang:We can walk together.↔我们一起走吧。 我们一起走吧。 Wǒmen yìqǐ zǒu ba.
				- Bai: Wonderful.↔好。 Hǎo.
		- 13.2
			- 中国城↔Chinatown (Zhōngguóchéng)
			- 成↔town; city (chéng)
			- 过↔Past completion (guo)

			- 拿↔to take; to get (ná)
			- 次↔measure word for frequency (cì)
			- 从↔from (cóng)
			- 一直↔straight; continuously (yìzhí)
			- 往↔towards (wǎng)
			- 南↔South (nán)
			- 路口↔intersection (lùkǒu)
			- 西↔west (xī)
			- 拐↔to turn (guǎi)
			- 哎↔exclamatory particle to express surprise or dissatisfaction (āi)
			- 东↔east (dōng)
			- 北↔North (běi)
			- 前↔Forward; ahead (qián)
			- 红绿灯↔traffic light (hónglǜdēng)
			- 灯↔light; lamp (dēng)
			- 右↔Right (yòu)
			- 左↔Left (zuǒ)
			- 前面↔Ahead; in front of (qiánmian)

				- Gao Wen Zhong: Let’s go to Chinatown to have some Chinese food.↔我们去中国城吃中国饭吧! 我们去中国城吃中国饭吧! Wǒmen qù Zhōngguóchéng chī Zhōngguó fàn ba!
				- Wang Peng: I’ve never been to Chinatown.↔我没去过中国城, Wǒ méi qù guo Zhōngguóchéng,

				- No problem. You drive, and I’ll tell you how to get there.↔没问题, 你开车, 我告诉你怎么走。 没问题, 你开车, 我告诉你怎么走。 Méi wèntí, nǐ kāi chē, wǒ gàosu nǐ zěnme zǒu.

				- turn right, and you’ll be there.→wǎng yòu yì guǎi jiù dào le. 往右一拐就到了。 往右一拐就到了。

		- 15.2
			- 感冒↔to have a cold gǎnmào
			- 生病↔to get sick shēng bìng
			- 身体↔body; health shēntǐ
			- 痒↔itchy yǎng
			- 过敏↔to be allergic to guòmǐn
			- 药店↔pharmacy yàodiàn
			- 健康↔healthy; health jiànkāng
			- 保险↔insurance bǎoxiân
			- 赶快↔right away; quickly; in a hurry gǎnkuài
			- 要不然↔otherwise yàobùrán
			- 越来越↔more and more yuè lái yuè
			- 上次↔last time shàng cì
			- 休息↔to take a break; to res txiūxi
			- 懒↔lazy lǎn
			- 再说↔moreover zàishuō
			- 乱↔randomly; arbitrarily; messily luàn
			- Dialogue
				- Wang Peng, what’s the matter?→Wáng Péng, nǐ zěnme le? 王朋, 你怎么了?

				- I haven’t been feeling well the last few days.↔zuìjìn zhè jǐ tiān shēntǐ hěn bù shūfu. 最近这几天身体很不舒服。 最近这几天身体很不舒服。
				- My eyes are red and itchy.↔Yǎnjing yòu hóng yòu yǎng. 眼睛又红又痒。 眼睛又红又痒。

				- I have so much homework this semester.↔Kěshì wǒ zhè ge xuéqī gōngkè hěn duō, 可是我这个学期功课多, 可是我这个学期功课很多,
				- Going to the doctor takes too much time.↔kàn yīshēng tài huā shíjiān. 看医生太花时间。 看医生太花时间。

				- I’d like to try some other medicines first.↔Wǒ xiǎng zài chī diǎnr bié de yāo shì shi. 我想再吃点儿别的要试试。 我想再吃点儿别的要试试。

				- After a couple days’ rest, I was fine.↔xiūxi liǎng tiān, zuìhòu yě hǎo le. 休息两天, 最后也好了。 休息两天, 最后也好了。b
				- No way, no way, you’re too lazy.↔Bù xíng, bù xíng, nǐ tài lǎn le. 不行, 不行, 你太懒了。 不行, 不行, 你太懒了。
				- Besides, you can’t just randomly take medicine by yourself.↔Zàishuō, nǐ bù néng zìjǐ luàn chī yào. 再说, 你不能自己乱吃药。 再说, 你不能自己乱吃药。

				- Wang Peng and Li You go to the same school.↔Wáng Péng gēn Lǐ Yǒu zài tóng yí ge xuéxiào xuéxí, 王朋跟李友在同一个学校学习,

				- I’m moving out of the dorm.↔wǒ yào cóng sùshè bān chu qu, 我要从宿舍搬出去, 我要从宿舍搬出去,
				- I have to clean and tidy up my room.↔děi dǎsǎo, zhěnglǐ fángjiān. 得打扫, 整理房间。 得打扫, 整理房间。
				- How about two weeks from now?→Nǐ kàn xià xià ge zhōumò, hǎo bù hǎo? 你看下下个周末, 好不好? 你看下下个周末, 好不好?
				- I’m sorry, two weeks from now would be even more impossible.↔Duìbuqǐ, xià xià ge zhōumò gèng bù xíng le, 对不起下下个周末更不行了, 对不起下下个周末更不行了,
				- I’m going on a trip to New York with my boyfriend.↔wǒ yào gēn wǒ de nánpéngyou qù Niǔyuē lǚxíng. 我要跟我的男朋友去纽约旅行。 我要跟我的男朋友去纽约旅行。
				- In that case…↔Nà… 那… 那…
				- Mr. Fei, I’m sorry,↔Fèi xiānshēng, duìbuqǐ, 费先生, 对不起, 费先生, 对不起,
				- My cell phone is out of power. Bye.→wǒ de shǒujī méi diàn le. Zàijiàn! 我的手机没电了。再见! 我的手机没电了。再见!
				- Hello… hello…↔Wèi… wèi… 喂… 喂… 喂… 喂…
		- 17.1
			- 吵↔chǎo to quarrel; noisy
			- 连↔lián even

			- 一房一厅↔yì fáng yì tīng one bedroom and one living room
			- 干净↔gān jìng clean

			- 那里↔nà li there
			- 安静↔ān jìng quiet
			- 房租↔fáng zū rent (n)
			- 元↔yuán (measure word for the basic Chinese monetary unit); yuan
			- 美元↔Měi yuán U.S. dollar
			- 人民币↔rén mín bì (RMB, Chinese currency)
			- 差不多↔chà bu duō almost; nearly; similar
			- 费↔fèi fee; expenses
			- 押金↔yā jīn security deposit
			- 当↔dāng to serve as; to be
			- 还↔huán to return (something)
			- 另外↔lìng wài furthermore; in addition
			- 准↔zhǔn to allow; to be allowed
			- 养↔yǎng to raise
			- 宠物↔chǒng wù pets
			- Dialogue
				- Wang Peng has been living in the school dorm for two semesters.↔Wáng Péng zài xuéxiào de sùshè zhù le liǎng ge xuéqī le.王朋在学校的宿舍住了两个学期了。
				- He thinks that the dorm is too noisy, and he can't sleep well. His room is too small, and he can't even fit a computer there. Besides, he has nowhere to cook. It's really inconvenient, so he plans to move out next semester.↔Tā juéde sùshè tài chǎo, shuì bù hǎo jiào, fángjiān tài xiǎo, lián diànnǎo dōu fàng bùxià, zàishuō yě méi yǒu dìfāng kěyǐ zuò fàn, hěn bù fāngbiàn, suǒyǐ zhǔnbèi xià gè xuéqí bān chūqù zhù.他觉得宿舍太 吵，睡不好觉，房间太小，连电脑都 放不下，再说 也没有地方可以做饭，很不方便，所以准备下个学期搬 出去住。
				- He has been looking for a place for a month now, but he hasn't found anything suitable yet.↔Tā zhǎo fángzi zhǎo le yí ge duō yuè le, kěshì hái méi yǒu zhǎo dào héshì de.他找房子找了一个多月了，可是还没有找到 合适的。
				- He just saw an ad in the newspaper saying there's an apartment for rent. It's very close to school, only a five-minute walk—very convenient.↔Gāngcái tā zài bàozhǐ shàng kàn dàole yí ge guǎnggào, shuō xuéxiào fùjìn yǒu yí tào gōngyù chūzū, lí xuéxiào hěn jìn, zǒulù zhǐyào wǔ fēnzhōng, hěn fāngbiàn.刚才他在报纸上看到了一个广告，说学校附近 有一套公寓出租，离学校很近，走路只要五分钟，很方便。
				- The apartment includes a bedroom, a kitchen, a bathroom, and a living room, and it's furnished.↔Gōngyù yǒu yí ge wò shì, yí ge chúfáng, yí ge wèishēngjiān, yí ge kètīng, hái dài jiājù.公寓有一个卧 室，一个厨房，一 个卫生间，一个客 厅，还带家具。
				- Wang Peng thinks this apartment may be just right for him.↔Wáng Péng juéde zhè tào gōngyù kěnéng duì tā hěn héshì.王朋觉得这套公寓可能对他很合适。
			- Homework
				- A: My apartment is very big. There is enough room for four people.→我的公寓很大。住得下四个人。
				- B: My room is small; it can’t even fit a big bed.↔我的房间很小，连一张大床都放不下。
				- A: The place where I live is close to the stores. It’s convenient to go shopping.↔我住的地方离商店很近。去买东西很方便。
				- B: Is that right? How long does it take to walk to the stores?→Shi ma? Zou lu qu shang dian yao duo chang shi jian? 是吗？走路去商店要多长时间？
				- A: It only takes three minutes to walk there.↔走路去商店只要三分钟。
				- A: You’ve been living here for a little over a month. How do you feel?→你在这儿^^住了一个多月了^^。你觉得怎么样？
				- B: I would like to move out.↔我想搬出去住。
				- A: What’s the matter?→怎么了？
				- B: It’s too noisy. I can’t get a good night’s sleep.↔太吵了。我^^睡不好觉^^。
		- 17.2
			- 一房一厅↔yì fáng yì tīng one bedroom and one living room
			- 干净↔gānjìng clean
			- 沙发↔shāfā sofa
			- 饭桌↔fànzhuō dining table
			- 椅子↔yǐzi chair
			- 书桌↔shūzhuō desk
			- 书架↔shūjià bookcase; bookshelf
			- 那里↔nàli there
			- 安静↔ānjìng quiet
			- 房租↔fángzū rent
			- 元↔yuán (measure word for the basic Chinese monetary unit); yuan
			- 美元↔Měiyuán U.S. dollar

			- 差不多↔chàbuduō almost; nearly; similar
			- 费↔fèi fee; expenses

			- 当↔dāng to serve as; to be
			- 还↔huán to return (something)
			- 另外↔lìngwài furthermore; in addition

			- Dialogue
				- Hi, do you have an apartment for rent?→Wéi, qǐng wèn nǐmen shì bú shì yǒu gōngyù chūzū?喂，请问你们是不是有公寓出租？
				- Yes, we do. One bedroom with a living room. It's very clean, and also furnished.↔Yǒu a, yì fáng yì tīng, fēicháng gānjìng, hái dài jiājù.有啊，一房一厅，非常干净，还带家具。
				- What kind of furniture does it have?→Yǒu shénme jiājù?有什么家具？
				- In the living room there is a sofa set, a dining table, and four chairs. The bedroom has a bed, a desk and a bookcase.↔Kètīng li yǒu yí tào shāfā, yì zhāng fànzhuō gēn sì bǎ yǐzi. Wòshì li yǒu yì zhāng chuáng, yì zhāng shūzhuō hé yí ge shūjià.客厅里有一套沙发，一张饭桌跟四把椅子。卧室里有一张床，一张书桌和一个书架。
				- Is it quiet over there?→Nǐmen nàli ānjìng bù ānjìng?你们那里安静不安静？
				- Extremely quiet.↔Fēicháng ānjìng.非常安静。
				- How much is the monthly rent?→Měi ge yuè fángzū duō shǎo qián?每个月房租多少钱？
				- Eight hundred and fifty dollars.↔Bābǎi wǔshí yuán.八百五十元。
				- 850 U.S. dollars? In renminbi that's almost… That's a little bit expensive. Could you come down a little bit?→Bābǎi wǔshí měi yuán? Rénmínbì chàbuduō shì. . . Yǒu yì diǎnr guì, néng bù néng piányì diǎnr?八百五十美元？人民币差不多是。。。有一点儿，能不能便宜点儿。
				- All right. You won't have to pay for the utilities.↔Nà nǐ búyòng fù shuǐ diàn fèi.那你不用付水电费。
				- Do I have to pay a deposit?→Yào bú yào fù yājīn?要不要付押金？
				- An extra month's rent as a security deposit, which will be returned to you when you move out. And another thing, no pets are allowed in our apartment.↔Yào duō fù yí ge yuè de fángzū dāng yājīn, bān chūqù de shíhou huán gěi nǐ. Lìngwài, wǒmen gōngyù bù zhǔn yǎng chǒngwù.要多付一个月的房租当押金，搬出去的时候还给你。另外，我们公寓不准养宠物。
				- That doesn't matter. I'm not interested in keeping pets. I dont't have pets of any kind.↔Méi guānxi, wǒ duì yǎng chǒngwù méi yǒu xìngqù, shénme chǒngwù dōu bù yǎng.没关系，我对养宠物没有兴趣，什么宠物都不养。
				- Great. Why don't you come over this afternoon and take a look?→Nà tài hǎo le. Nǐ jīntiān xiàwǔ lái kàn kan ba.那太好了。你今天下午来看看吧。
				- Ok.↔Hǎo.好。
			- Homework
				- 1. A: This living room is so clean.↔这个客厅非常干净。
				- B: It’s too clean! It has nothing (in it,) not even a piece of furniture or a piece of paper.↔太干净了！里面什么东西都没有，连一个家具或者一张纸都没有。
				- 2. A: What are you interested in?→你对什么有兴趣？
				- B: I am interested in Keeping pets.↔我对养宠物有兴趣。
				- 3. I’ve been living with my friend for more than two years.↔我跟我的朋友一起住了两年多了。
				- Our apartment is furnished and very close to school, the park, and the bus stop.↔我们的公寓带家具，离学校，公园和公共汽车站都很近。
				- The rent is less expensive than living in the dorm.↔房租没有住在宿舍里那么贵。
				- I like where I live.↔我喜欢我住的地方。
				- My friend is also very nice to me.↔我的朋友也对我很好。
				- He cleans the house once a week and often hosts dance parties.↔他每个星期打扫一次房子，他也常常开舞会。
				- Even my mother likes the place I live in.↔连我妈妈都喜欢我住的地方。
				- But I may have to move out next semester.↔可是下个学期我可能要搬出去。
				- It’s not because it’s so noisy that I cannot sleep well, and it’s not because I am allergic to my friend’s dog.↔不是因为太吵，我睡不好觉，也不是因为我对我朋友的狗过敏。
				- It’s because my friend’s cousin is moving in and the place is too small to house three people.↔因为我朋友的表姐要搬进来了。这个地方太小，住不下三个人。
				- It’s difficult to find a suitable and affordable apartment.↔找到一套又合适又便宜的公寓很难。
				- I’m thinking I could ask my friend if he would like to find a house that’s a little bigger.↔我想我会去问我的朋友他想不想找一个大一点儿的房子。
		- 18.1
			- 当然↔dāngrán of course
			- 胖↔pàng fat
			- 怕↔pà to fear
			- 简单↔jiǎndān simple
			- 跑步↔pǎo bù to jog
			- 跑↔pǎo to run
			- 难受↔nánshòu hard to bear; uncomfortable
			- 网球↔wǎngqiú tennis
			- 拍↔pāi racket
			- 篮球↔lánqiú basketball
			- 游泳↔yóu yǒng to swim
			- 危险↔wēixiǎn dangerous
			- 淹死↔yān sǐ to drown
			- 愿意↔yuànyì to be willing
			- Dialogue
				- Look, my gut is getting bigger and bigger.↔Nǐ kàn, wǒ de dùzi yuè lái yuè dà le.你看，我的肚子越来越大了。
				- You usually overeat, and on top of that you don't exercise; of course you're putting on more and more weight.↔Nǐ píngcháng chī de nàme duō, yòu bú yùndòng, dāngrán yuè lái yuè pàng le.你平常吃的那么多，又不运动，当然越来越胖了。
				- What should I do?→Nà zěnme bàn ne?那怎么办呢？
				- If you're afraid of being overweight, you should exercise two or three times a week, for half an hour each time. Then your belly will get smaller.↔Rúguǒ pà pàng, nǐ yí ge xīngqī yùndòng liǎng, sān cì, měi cì bàn ge xiǎoshí, dùzi jiù huì xiǎo le.如果怕胖，你一个星期运动两，三次，每次半个小时，肚子就会小了。
				- I haven't exercised for two years. What kind of exercise should I do?→Wǒ liǎng nián méi yùndòng le, zuò shénme yùndòng ne?我两年没运动了，做什么运动呢？
				- The simplest exercise is jogging.↔Zuì jiǎndān de yùndòng shì pǎo bù.最简单的运动是跑步。
				- It's so cold in winter, and so hot in summer. Jogging is too uncomfortable.↔Dōngtiān nàme lěng, xiàtiān nàme rè, pǎo bù tài nánshòu le.冬天那么冷，夏天那么热，跑步太难受了。
				- How about playing tennis?→Nǐ dǎ wǎngqiú ba.你打网球吧。
				- Then I'd have to get a tennis racket, and tennis shoes. You know tennis rackets, and tennis shoes are very expensive!↔Dǎ wǎngqiú děi mǎi wǎngqiú pāi, wǎng qiú xié, nǐ zhī dào, wǎng qiú pāi, wǎngqiú xié guì jí le!打网球得买网球拍，网球鞋，你知道，网球拍，网球鞋贵极了！
				- How about getting a few people together to play basketball? Buying a basketball is very inexpensive.↔Zhǎo jǐ ge rén dǎ lán qiú ba. Mǎi ge lán qiú hěn piányì.找几个人打篮球吧。买个篮球很便宜。
				- Then I'd have to call people and arrange to meet, that's way too much hassle.↔Nà měi cì dōu děi dǎ diànhuà yuē rén, máfàn sǐ le.那每次都得打电话约人，麻烦死了。
				- Then why don't you swim? There's no need to look for people, it wouldn't cost much money, and you could go any time.↔Nǐ qù yóu yǒng ba. Búyòng zhǎo rén, yě búyòng huā hěn duō qián, shénme shíhou qù dōu kěyǐ.你去游泳吧。不用找人，也不用花很多钱，什么时候去都可以。
				- Swimming? I'm afraid of water, that's too dangerous. What if I drown?→Yóu yǒng? wǒ pà shuǐ, Tài wēixiǎn le, yān sǐ le zěnme bàn?游泳？我的水。太危险了，淹死了怎么办？
				- There's nothing I can do to help. If you're not willing to exercise, then keep packing on the pounds.↔Wǒ yě méi bànfǎ le. Nǐ bú yuànyì yùndòng, nà jiù pàng xià qù ba.我也没办法了。你不愿意运动，那就胖下去吧。
			- Homework
				- 1. A: Why don’t you like to swim? Are you afraid of water?→为什么你不喜欢游泳？你怕水吗？
				- B: Of course not. I feel it’s too much trouble to go swimming.↔当然不怕。我觉得游泳太麻烦了。
				- 2. A: You studied dancing for three years. Why didn’t you continue?→你 学跳舞学了三年。（or 你学了三年的舞。）为什么^^没学下去^^？
				- B: I was too tired, and I was not willing to continue.↔我太累了，我也^^不愿意学下去了^^。
				- 3. A: How long has it been since you danced?→你^^多长时间^^没跳舞了？
				- B: It’s been more than six months.↔六个多月了。
				- 4. I have studied Chinese for more than seven months.↔我^^学中文学了七个多月了^^。（or 我学了七 个多月的中文了。）
				- My teacher asked us to listen to the audio recordings for half an hour every day.↔我的老师让我们每天都听半个小时的录音。
				- But I haven’t done so for more than a week.↔可是我一个星期没听了。
				- There’s a test tomorrow. I’d better review thoroughly and hope that I will ace the test.↔明天我有一个考试。我得好好复习，希望明天我能考得很好。
		- 18.2
			- 为了↔wèile for the sake of
			- 提高↔tígāo to improve, raise, heighten
			- 水平↔shuǐpíng level; standard
			- 足球↔zúqiú soccer; football
			- 比赛↔bǐsài game; match; competition; to compete
			- 国际↔guójì international
			- 美式↔měishì American-style
			- 脚↔jiǎo foot
			- 应该↔yīnggāi should
			- 踢↔tī to kick
			- 抱↔bào to hold or carry in arms
			- 压↔yā to press; hold down; weigh down
			- 被↔bèi by
			- 棒↔bàng fantastic; super
			- 运动服↔yùndòngfú sportswear
			- 担心↔dānxīn to worry
			- 着↔zhe particle, continuation of action/state
			- Dialogue
				- Wang Peng's younger sister, Wang Hong, just came from Beijing. She will be going to college in the United States. Right now she is staying at Gao Xiaoyin's place, studying English. To improve her English, she watches two hours of TV every day.↔Wáng Péng de mèimei Wáng Hóng gāng cóng Běijīng lái, yào zài Měiguó shàng dàxué, xiànzài zhù zài Gāo XiǎoYīn jiā li xué Yīngwén. Wéi?e tígāo Yīngwén shuǐpíng, tā měi tiān dōu kàn liǎng ge xiǎoshí de diànshì.王朋的妹妹王红刚从北京来，要在 美国上大学，现在住在高小音家 里学英文。为了提高英文水平， 她每天都看两个小时的电视。
				- Hurry, turn the TV on. The football game is starting.↔Kuài bǎ diànshì dǎ kāi, zúqiú bǐsài kāishǐ le.快把电视打开，足球比赛开始 了。
				- Really? I like watching football games too…What kind of football is this? How come it's not round?→Shì ma? Wǒ yě xǐhuan kàn zúqiú sài …Zhè shì shénme zúqiú a? Zěnme bú shì yuán de?是吗？我也喜欢看足球赛。 …这是什么足球 啊？怎么不是 圆的？
				- This is not international football, this is American football.↔Zhè bú shì guójì zúqiú, zhè shì Měishì zúqiú.这不是国际足球，这是美式足 球。
				- To play football you should kick (the ball) with your feet. Why is that guy running with the ball in his hands?→Zúqiú yīnggāi yòng jiǎotī , wèishénme nà ge rén yòng shǒu bào zhen pǎo ne?足球应该用脚踢，为什么那个人 用手抱着跑呢？
				- In American football you can use your hands.↔Měishì zúqiú kěyǐ yòng shǒu.美式足球可以用手。
				- Look! All those people are piling on top of each other. Wouldn't the people underneath be crushed to pieces?→nǐ kàn, nǐ kàn, nàmeduō rén dōu yā zài yìqǐ , xiàmian de rén bú shì yào bèi yā huài le ma?你看，你看，那么多人都压在一 起，下面的人不是要被压坏了吗？
				- Don't worry, they're really strong. Besides, they wear special sports clothing, so everything's fine.↔Bié dānxīn, tāmen de shēntǐ dōu hěn bàng, érqiě hái chuān tèbié de yùndòngfú, méi wèntí别担心，他们的身体都很棒，而 且还穿特别的运动服，没问题。
				- I"ve been watching for a while and I still don't get it. Let's watch something else.↔Wǒ kàn le bàntiān yě kàn bu dǒng. Háishi kàn bié de ba.我看了半天y也看不懂。还是看别 的吧。
				- You only have to live in America for half a year before you will begin to like American football.↔Nǐ zài Měiguó zhù bànnián jiù huì xǐhuan le. Wǒ nánpéngyou kàn Měishì zúqiú de shíhou, chángcháng lián fàn dōu wàng le chī .你在美国住半年就会喜欢了。我 男朋友看美式足球的时候，常常 连饭都忘了吃。
			- Homework
				- A: The weather is getting colder and colder. You’d better put on some more clothes. Otherwise, you may catch a cold.↔天气越来越冷。你最好多穿一些衣服。要不然，你会感冒。
				- B: Don’t worry. I am in great physical condition. I don’t get sick easily. 别担心。我的身体非常好。我不容易生病。
				- 2. A: How come my tennis ball is not round any more?→我的网球怎么不圆了(怎么不是圆的了）？
				- B: I am sorry. It’s got crushed by the sofa.↔对不起。你的网球被沙发压坏了。
				- 3. A: Class, I have a fever. Today I have to give the lesson sitting down.↔同学们，我发烧了。今天我得坐着上课。
				- B: Teacher, you should go home and rest.↔老师，你应该回家休息。
				- 4. A: Old Wang, do you know how to send text messages?→老王，你知道怎么发短信吗
				- B: I don’t. I don’t even know how to email.↔我不知道。我连电子邮件都不知道怎么发。
				- A: Old Wang, you don’t even have a cell phone, right?→老王，你连手机都没有，对不对？
				- B: Right!↔对！
			-
		- 19.1
			- 马上↔mǎshàng immediately; right away
			- 放假↔fàng jià go on vacation; have time off
			- 公司↔gōngsī company
			- 实习↔shíxí to intern
			- 打工↔dǎ gōng to work at a temporary job (often part time)
			- 计划↔jìhuà plan; to plan (formal)
			- 暑假↔shǔjià summer vacation
			- 打算↔dǎsuàn to plan; plan (col.)
			- 父母↔fùmǔ parents; dad and mom
			- 首都↔shǒudū capital city
			- 政治↔zhèngzhì politics
			- 文化↔wénhuà culture
			- 名胜古迹↔míngshèng gǔjì famous scenic spots and historic sites
			- 有名↔yǒumíng famous; well-known
			- 导游↔dǎoyóu tour guide
			- 护照↔hùzhào passport
			- 订↔dìng to reserve; to book (ticket, hotel)
			- 签证↔qiānzhèng visa
			- 旅行社↔lǚxíngshè travel agency
			- 长城↔chángchéng the Great Wall
			- 香港↔xiānggǎng Hong Kong
			- 台北↔táiběi Taipei
			- What plans do you have this summer?→Zai fang jia, ni you shen me ji hua?
			- Dialogue
				- Li You, time flies, it'll be break soon, some of our classmates are going to summer school; some of them are going to intern at different companies; some will go home and work. What are your plans?→Lǐ Yǒu, shíjiān guò de zhēn kuài, mǎshàng jiù yào fàng jià le, wǒmen de tóngxué, yǒu de qù shǔqī bān xuéxí, yǒu de qù gōngsī shíxí, yǒu de huí jiā dǎ gōng, nǐ yǒu shénme jì huà? 李友，时间过得真快，马上就要放假了，我们的同学，有的去暑期班学习，有的去公司实习，有的回家打工，你有什么计划？
				- I haven't decided. What about you Wang Peng?→Wǒ hái méi yǒu xiǎng hǎo. Nǐ ne, Wáng Péng? 我还没有想好。你呢，王朋？
				- I plan to go back to Beijing to see my parents.↔Wǒ shǔjià dǎsuàn huí Běiīng qù kàn fùmǔ. 我暑假打算回北京去看父母。
				- Really? I hear that Beijing is a really interesting city.↔Shì ma? Wǒ tīngshuō Běijīng zhège chéngshì hěnyǒuyìsi. 是吗？我听说北京这个城市很有意思。
				- Of course. Beijing is China's capital, and it's also China's political and cultural center, with lots of famous historic sites.↔Dāng rán. Běijīng shì Zhōngguó de shǒudū, yě shì Zhōngguó de zhèngzhì, wénhuà zhōngxīn, yǒu hěn duō míngshèng gǔjì. 当然。北京是中国的首都，也是中国的政治，文化中心，有很多名胜古迹。
				- That's right. The Great Wall is very famous.↔Duì a, Chángchéng hěn yǒumíng. 对啊，长城很有名。
				- And there are tons of great restaurants in Beijing.↔Háiyǒu, Běijīng de hǎo fànguǎn duō de bù déliǎo. 还有，北京的好饭馆多得不得了。
				- Really? I've been to Hong Kong and Taipei, but I've never been to Beijing. I wish I could go to Beijing.↔Zhēn de? Wǒ qù guò Xiānggǎng, Táiběi, hái méi qù guò Běijīng, yàoshi néng qù Běijīng jiù hǎo le. 真的？我去过香港，台北，还没去过北京，要是能去北京就好了。
				- Why don't you go with me? I could be your guide.↔Nà nǐ gēn wǒ yìqǐ qù ba, wǒ dāng nǐ de dǎoyóu. 那你跟我一起，我当你的导游。
				- Really? That would be great! I already have a passport. I'll have to apply for a visa at once.↔Zhēn de ma? Nà tài hǎo le! Hùzhào wǒ yǐjīng yǒu le. Wǒ děi gǎnkuài bàn qiānzhèng. 真的吗？那太好了！护照我已经有了，我得赶快办签证。
				- I'll give the travel agency a call right away and get the plane tickets.↔Nà wǒ mǎshàng gě lǚxíngshè dǎ diànhuà dìng fēijī piào. 那我马上给旅行社打电话订飞机票。
		- 19.2
			- 初↔chū beginning
			- 单程↔dānchéng one-way trip
			- 往返↔wǎngfǎn make a round trip (verb)
			- 航空↔hángkōng aviation
			- 查↔chá to check; to look into
			- 航班↔hángbān scheduled flight
			- 千↔qiān thousand
			- 直飞↔zhí fēi fly directly
			- 打折↔dǎ zhé to sell at discount
			- 转机↔zhuǎn jī change plans
			- 靠↔kào to lean on; to lean against; to be next to
			- 窗户↔chuānghu window
			- 走道↔zǒudào aisle
			- 份↔fèn mw for meal order; job
			- 素餐↔sùcān vegetarian meal
			- 旅馆↔lǚguǎn hotel
			- 中国国际航空公司↔zhōngguó guójì hángkōng gōngsī Air China
			- 西北航空公司↔xīběi hángkōng gōngsī Northwest Airlines
			- Dialogue
				- Tianyi Travel Agency, good morning.↔Tiān Yī lǚxíngshè, nǐ hǎo. 天一旅行社，你好。
				- Good morning. How much is a ticket to Beijing for the beginning of June?→Nǐ hǎo. Qǐng wèn liùyuè chū dào Běijīng de jīpiào duōshǎo qián? 你好。请问六月初到北京的机票多少钱？
				- One way or round trip?→Nín yào mǎi dānchéng piào háishi wǎngfǎn piào? 您要买单程票还是往返票？
				- Two round trip tickets.↔Wǒ yào mǎi liǎng zhāng wǎngfǎn piào. 我要买两张往返票。
				- Which airline?→Nǐ xiǎng mǎi nǎ jiā hángkōng gōngsī _de_ (feiji piao)? 你想买哪家航空公司的？
				- I'll get whichever airline is the least expensive.↔Nǎ jiā de piányì, jiù mǎi nǎ jiā de. 哪家的便宜，就买哪家的。
				- Please wait a moment. Let me check. Quite a few airlines fly there. Air China, $1,500, direct flight. Northwest is having a sale. About $1,460, but you have to change planes.↔Qǐng děng deng, wǒ chá yí xià. . . hǎo jǐ jiā hángkōng gōngsī dōu yǒu hángbān. Zhōngguó Guójì Hángkōng Gōngsī, yì qiān wǔ, zhífēi. Xīběi Hángkōng Gōngsī zhèngzài dǎ zhé, chàbuduō yì qiān sì bǎi liùshí, kěshì yào zhuǎn jī. 请等等，我查一下。。。好几家航空公司都有航班。中国国际航空公司，一千五，直飞。西北航空公司正在打折，差不多一千四百六十，可是要转机。
				- Northwest is only $40 cheaper than China Airlines, I'll go with China Airlines.↔Xīběi zhǐ bǐ Guóháng piányì sìshí jǐ kuài qián, wǒ háishi mǎi guóháng ba. 西北只比国航便宜四十几块钱，我还是买国航吧。
				- What are the dates for departure and return?→Nǎ yì tiān zǒu? Nǎ yì tiān huí lái? 哪一天走？哪一天回来？
				- Departing on June 10, returning on July 15. Can I reserve seats now?→Liùyuè shí hào zǒu, qīyuè shíwǔ hào huí lái. Xiànzài kěyǐ dìng wèizi ma? 六月十号走，七月十五号回来。现在可以订位子吗？
				- Yes, you can. Do you prefer window or aisle seats?→Kěyǐ. Nǐmen xǐhuan kào chuānghu de háishi kào zǒudào de? 可以。你们喜欢靠窗户的还是靠走道的？
				- Aisle seats. Oh, that's right, my friend is a vegetarian. Could you please order vegetarian meals for her?→Kào zǒudào de. Duì le, wǒ péngyou chī sù, máfan bāng tā dìng yí fèn sùcān. 靠走道的。对了，我朋友吃素，麻烦帮她订一份素餐。
				- No problem. While in Beijing, do you need to make reservations for a hotel or car rental?→Méi wèntí. . . nín zài Běijīng yào dìng lǚguǎn, zū chē ma? 没问题。。。您在北京要订旅馆，租车吗？
				- No, thank you.↔Búyòng, xièxie! 不用，谢谢！
		- 20.1
			- 行李↔xíngli luggage
			- 托运↔tuōyùn to check (luggage)
			- 包↔bāo bag;sack; bundle; package
			- 箱子↔xiāngzi suitcase; box
			- 超重↔chāozhòng to be overweight (of luggage, freight, etc.)
			- 超↔chāo to exceed; to surpass
			- 登机牌↔dēng jī pái boarding pass
			- 牌↔pái plate; tablet; card
			- 登机口↔dēng jī kǒu boarding gate
			- 口↔kǒu opening; entrance; mouth
			- 哭↔kū to cry; to weep
			- 地↔de (particle to link adverbial and verb)
			- 照顾↔zhàogu to look after; to care for; to attend to
			- 起飞↔qǐfēi (of airplanes) to take off
			- 小心↔xiǎoxīn to be careful
			- 一路平安↔yīlù píng'ān have a good trip; bon voyage
			- 乱跑↔Luan pao run around
			- Dialogue
				- Miss, these are our tickets.↔Xiǎojiě, zhè shì wǒmen de jīpiào. 小姐，这是我们的机票。
				- Please show me your passports. How many pieces of checked luggage do you have?→Qǐng bǎ hùzhào gěi wǒ kàn kàn. Nǐmen yǒu jǐ jiàn xínglǐ yào tuōyùn? 请把护照给我看看。 你们有几件行李要 托运？
				- Two. We won't check this bag. We'll take it on board.↔Liǎng jiàn. Zhège bāo bù tuōyùn, wǒmen dài shàng fēijī. 两件。这个包不托 运，我们带上飞机。
				- Please put the suitcases up here.↔Máfan nín bǎ xiāngzi ná shànglái. 麻烦您把箱子拿 上来。
				- Miss, they are not over the weight limit, I hope.↔Xiǎojiě, méi chāozhòng ba? 小姐，没超重吧？
				- No, they're not. Here are your passports and tickets. These are your boarding passes. Please go to Gate 5 to board the plane.↔Méiyǒu. Zhè shì nǐmen de hùzhào, jīpiào, zhè shì dēng jī pái. Qǐng dào wǔ hào dēng jī kǒushàng fēijī. 没有。这是你们的护照、 机票，这是登机牌。请到五号登机口上飞机。
				- Thanks.↔Xièxiè. 谢谢。
				- You're both leaving for Beijing. I'll be all alone here↔Gēgē, nǐmen qù Běijīngle, jiù wǒ yí ge rén zài zhè'er. 哥哥，你们去北京了，就 我一个人在这儿。
				- Xiao Hong, don't cry. We'll be back in just a few weeks. Work hard on your English. Don't go running around.↔Xiǎo hóng, bié kū, wǒmen jǐ gè xīng qī jiù huílái, nǐ hǎohǎo er dìxué Yīngwén, bié luàn pǎo. 小红，别哭，我们几个星 期就回来，你好好儿地学英文，别乱跑。
				- Be back in a few weeks? Won't be back till a few weeks later!↔Búshì jǐ gè xīngqí jiù huílái, shì jǐ gè xīngqí yǐhòu cái huílái. 不是几个星期就回来，是 几个星期以后才回来。
				- Don't worry. My sister Xiaoyin will take good care of you.↔Bié dānxīn, wǒ jiějiě xiǎo yīn huì zhàogù nǐ. 别担心，我姐姐小音会照 顾你。
				- That's right. Don't worry.↔Duì, bié dānxīn. 对，别担心。
				- When does the plane leave?→Fēijī jǐ diǎn qǐfēi? 飞机几点起飞？
				- 12:00 noon. There are two hours left.↔Zhōngwǔ shí'èr diǎn, hái yǒu liǎng gè duō xiǎoshí. 中午十二点，还有两个多小时。
				- Bai Ying'ai, when are you going to New York for your internship?→Bái Yīng'ài, nǐ shénme shíhòu qù Niǔyuē shíxí? 白英爱，你什么时候去纽约实习？
				- I'm not going to New York anymore. Wenzhong helped me get an internship in California.↔Wǒ bú qù Niǔyuēle. Wénzhōng bāng wǒ zài jiāzhōu zhǎole yī fèn shíxí gōngzuò. 我不去纽约了。文中帮我 在加州找了一份实习工 作。
				- That's right. We're driving to California next week.↔Duì, wǒmen xià gè xīngqí kāichē qù jiāzhōu. 对，我们下个星期开车去加州。
				- Really? Driving and sightseeing at the same time, that's really wonderful.↔Shì ma? Yībiān er kāichē, yībiān er wánr, tài hǎo le. 是吗？一边儿开车，一边儿玩儿，太好了。
				- Drive carefully. Have fun!↔Kāichē xiǎoxīn. Zhù nǐmen wánr dé gāoxìng. 开车小心。祝你们玩儿得高兴。
				- Have a safe trip. Don't forget to email us after you arrive in Beijing.↔Zhù nǐmen yīlù píng'ān. Dàole Běijīng yǐhòu, bié wàngle gěi wǒmen fā gè diànzǐ yóujiàn. 祝你们一路平安。到了北京以后，别忘了给我们发个电子邮件。
				- OK. See you in the fall then.↔Hǎo, nà wǒmen qiūtiān jiàn. 好，那我们秋天见。
				- See you next semester.↔Xià gè xuéqí jiàn. 下个学期见。
				- Goodbye!↔Zàijiàn! 再见!
		- 20.2
			- 叔叔↔shūshu uncle
			- 阿姨↔āyí aunt
			- 欢迎↔huānyíng to welcome
			- 瘦↔shòu thin, slim (usually of a person or animal); lean
			- 爷爷↔yéye paternal grandfather
			- 奶奶↔nǎinai paternal grandmother
			- 烤鸭↔kǎoyā roas duck
			- 首都机场↔Shǒudū Jīchǎng the Capital Airport (in Beijing)
			- Dialogue
				- Xiao Peng!↔Xiǎo péng! 小朋！
				- Dad, Mom!↔Bà, mā! 爸，妈！
				- You Must be really tired.↔Lèi huàile ba? 累坏了吧？
				- Not really. Dad, Mom, let me introduce you… This is my classmate Li You.↔Hái hǎo. Bà, mā, wǒ gěi nǐmen jièshào yíxià, zhè shì wǒ de tóngxué Lǐ Yǒu. 还好。爸，妈，我给 你们介绍一下，这是 我的同学李友。
				- Uncle, Aunt, how do you do?→Shūshu, āyí, nǐmen hǎo. 叔叔，阿姨，你们好。
				- Welcome to Beijing.↔Huānyíng nǐ lái Běijīng. 欢迎你来北京。
				- Li You, you speak Chinese wonderfully.↔Lǐ Yǒu, nǐ de zhōngwén shuō dé zhēn hǎo. 李友，你的中文说得真好。
				- Thank you. It's because Wang Peng is a good teacher.↔Xièxiè. Shì yīnwèi wángpéngjiào dé hǎo. 谢谢。是因为王朋教得好。
				- You flatter me. It's because you're smart.↔Nǎlǐ, shì yīnwèi nǐ cōngmíng. 哪里，是因为你聪明。
				- Hey, you're both smart.↔Āi, nǐmen liǎ dōu cōngmíng. 哎，你们俩都聪明。
				- Xiao Peng, you seem to have lost some weight. Is it because you were too busy working and had no time to eat?→Xiǎo péng, nǐ hǎoxiàng shòule diǎnr. Shì búshì dǎgōng tài máng, méi yǒu shíjiān chīfàn? 小朋，你好像瘦了点儿。是不是打工太忙，没有时 间吃饭?
				- Mom, I haven't lost any weight. I exercise a lot. I'm much stronger than before.↔Wǒ méi shòu. Wǒ chángcháng yùndòng, shēntǐ bǐ yǐqián bàng duōle. 我没瘦。我常常运动，身体比以前棒多了。
				- How is Xiao Hong?→Xiǎo hóng zěnmeyàng? 小红怎么样？
				- She's great. Her English has really improved.↔Tā hěn hǎo, Yīngwén shuǐpíng tígāole hěnduō. 她很好，英文水平提高了很多。
				- Let's go. We'll talk at leisure after we get in the car. Grandpa and Grandma are waiting for us at the roast duck restaurant.↔Zǒu ba, wǒmen shàng chē yǐhòu, zài màn man er de liáo ba. Yéyé, nǎi nǎi zài kǎoyā diàn děng wǒmen ne! 走吧，我们上车以后，再慢慢儿地聊吧。爷爷、奶 奶在烤鸭店等我们呢！
				- Roast duck restaurant?→Kǎoyā diàn? 烤鸭店？

		- Oral Test Practice, Sample Sentences
			- 15 Allergies
				- Wo yanjiang hong hong de, yang yang de
				- Wo dui hua guomin
				- Ruguo ni bu shu fu
				- Wo kan bing
				- Wo de duzi teng si le
				- Wo de duzi teng qi lai
				- Wo tou teng (headache)
				- Wo ganmao le
				- Wo fashou le
				- Ni yi ge xing qi chi san ci, yi ci chi er pian?
				- Meitian san ci, yi ci liang pian.
				- Ni yi ge xing qi yun dong ji ci?
				- Ni yi ci yun dong duo chang shijian?
				- Ni yi ge xingqi ting ji ci lu yin?
					- Wo yi ge xing qi ting san ci lu ying
				- Qing yi ge xing qi da sao liang ci wo de fang jian
				- Zenmeban
			- Wo san ge yue da sao le san ci wo de fangjian
			- Wo renshi ta yijing shi liu nian le. Ta shi wo de didi, suoyi ta sheng de shihou wo jiu renshi ta le
			- Impressions
				- Wo dui Niu Yue de yinxiang buhao. Niu yue tai duo ren, tai duo che le.
				- Gao wen zhong gei wo de yini xiang hen hao. Ta hen gao, hen shuai, ye hen congming
				- Ni gaosu ni de peng you zen me zuo dui xue zhong wen you yong?

	- Lecture 6 [February 20th, 2021](Daily Document/February 20th, 2021.md)
		- Pointers
			- ```c
int x = 1, y = 2, z[10];
int *ip; /* ip is a pointer to int */

ip = &x; /* ip now points to x */

y = *ip; /* y is now 1 */
*ip = 0; /* x is now 0 */

ip = &z[0]; /* ip now points to z[0] */
```
            - Static variables for global variables
    - Lecture 7 [February 26th, 2021](Daily Document/February 26th, 2021.md)
        - Use assert to check malloc does not return null
            - ```c
s2 = malloc(sizeof(char) * strlen(s)+1));
assert(s2);
```
        - free often
            - ```c
// make a copy of a string constant to modify it
char *copy = allocStrcpy("hi there!");

puts(copy);
copy[0] = 'b';
puts(copy);

// don't do this, clobbers malloc header
// strcpy(copy - 12, "ha ha i destroy your data");

free(copy);

// don't do this, already freed
// copy[1] = 'o';
// puts(copy);

// 0x12 is not a legal address to write to
// strcpy((char *) 0x12, "hi");
```

    - Commands
        - ssh bmw52@node.zoo.cs.yale.edu
        - scp file.c bmw52@node.zoo.cs.yale.edu:~/cs223/
        - Compile file
            - The first line is the command to compile the program. The dollar sign is my prompt, which is printed by the system to tell me it is waiting for a command. The command calls gcc as c99 with arguments -g3 (enable maximum debugging info), -o (specify executable file name, otherwise defaults to a.out), count (the actual executable file name), and count.c (the source file to compile). This tells gcc that we should compile count.c to count in C99 mode with maximum debugging info included in the executable file.
                - ```bash
c99 -g3 -Wall -o count count.c && ./count
`````` -- None -- 
 ./count
```

- Math 225
    - Lecture 1 [February 2nd, 2021](Daily Document/February 2nd, 2021.md)
        - Euler's rotation theorem↔If you rotate a sphere in a rigid way, you will arrive at the same shape 
        - Linear regression, poly-fit
        - Vector
            - Array of numbers (CS notation)
            - Magnitude and direction (Physical notation)
            - Elements in a vector space
        - Vector Space↔A vector space $V$  over field $F$  is a set equipped with two operations-addition and scalar multiplication
            - addition↔For every $x,y\in V$  there exists a unique element $x+y\in V$ 
            - scalar multiplication→For every element $x\in V$ , there exists $\lambda \in F$  such that $\lambda x \in V$ 
            - These operations satisfy the following (8 axioms) ↓ 
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/89UhprpuEjYWzRO1PCf6g4NWdkV3G65Jq91Ww6KSMJLkncQjPsZpY1A9OoQ7tmGhCCGy9Q_m03zlWR_kCS-FD07RadtgzFxJC4oOCiUanObCCChN4IAOlex23UzNhMoY.png)
            - Remarks ↓ 
                - Elements in $V$ are called vectors and elements in $F$  are called scalars
                - A vector space is a tuple ($V, F, +, \cdot)$
                - Associativity implies we may write $x+y+z$
    - Lecture 2 [February 5th, 2021](Daily Document/February 5th, 2021.md)
        - Sets↔A type of collection of elements
            - Order {{ does not }} matter
            - $\{4,2,1,3\} = \{1,1,1,2,3,4\}$
        - Two sets are disjoint if↔{{ }}$A \cap B = \phi$ 
        - New Set Notations/Operations
            - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/5hd7NL_JEKs9xa_Mrzr32LWPE2hfsT7gixvo8xsm7Qm9RLLK6ciWq4BA_9rY_p8W42SY0oV7jIcNQGa70div-whXS9heVsfHMDns1RkMClFqHXdx86Xc7vKs_HuMtcyq.png)→subset, but not equal to (strictly smaller and contained within) 
            - $\phi$→the empty set
                - For any set $A$ , $\phi$ $\subseteq$ $A$ {{  }}
            - x→Matrix multiplication
                - A x B = $\{(a, b) | a \in A, b \in B\}$
        - Functions $f:A \to B$
            - domain in this example→$A$ 
            - codomain in this example→$B$ 
            - image→$f(A) = \{f(a | a \in A\}$ 
            - difference between codomain and image→codomain is  everything that can result, range is everything that actually results 
        - Fields
            - A field $F$  is a set equipped with two operations, {{ addition }} and {{ multiplication }}
            - Multiplication is different from a vector field
            - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/LUJp6U8fZfGdsU-JLLGAXZcQa1ZetZK_hLlwf2jOCi8j2Fkeycsakz7lDuH79Q8MfNQhoQrerFxfNcRqXuRLGe0dnSYjzhvyRIm63mP6N047FKPAOqGI4apRjehTnFEe.png)
            - Questions
                - Is $R$  a field? Yes
                - Is $Q$  a field? Yes
                - Is $C$  a field? Yes
                - Is $Q(\sqrt 2) = \{a + b\sqrt 2 | a, b \in Q\}$  a field? Yes
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/M7Hp7KR2H9feGcQIX6ZUnnxm7iajd-lCMRkYfSSXSgwk6uPHX4d1yxdOqHhBX8jaYjlk9VkiOL_0FztA8vCIokg8PhvNv0ViutDsBXrl9q_7vPbavsMZaKg7UGL7fmcR.png)
                - Non-Fields
                    - $N$  - no inverses
                    - $Z$  - no mult inverse
                    - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/OIJ485du_5sNdge6a3L35SoiY7xvFVzmv_NpVXymW3k63_Jm4t9trPwOIrqqbfEgy-XAbPcNx0hHLIt0Rp9TV9TB-7bPDPTr6r09SvCvSl4TPMgwnlMxCC2tdc93XiPn.png) - not closed under set
        - Theorems → Propositions → Lemmas
        - Lemma (Cancellation Law)↔Let $F$  be a field and let $a,b,c\in F$ . 1) If $a+c=b+c$ , then $a=b$ . 2) If $c\neq 0$  and $a\cdot c = b \cdot c$ , then $a=b$ . 
    - TA Session [February 6th, 2021](Daily Document/February 6th, 2021.md)
        - Logic
        - Statesmant S can be
            - True
            - False
            - Neither true nor false, like this statement is false
            - True and false
        - Not operator \↔A \ B means everything in A not in B
        - De Morgan's Law
            - $A$  \ $(B \cup C)$  = $(A\backslash B) \cap (A \backslash C)$
    - Lecture 3[February 10th, 2021](Daily Document/February 10th, 2021.md)
        - [Vector Space](Second Semester/Math 225/Lecture 1 February 2nd, 2021/Vector Space.md)
            - Examples
                - Prototypical (generic) example↔$F^n = \{(a_1,...,a_n) | a_1,...,a_n \in F\}$ 
                    - $\forall a = (a_1, ..., a_n), b=(b_1,...,b_n)$  , $a+b=(a_1+b_1, ..., a_n+b_n)$
                    - $\forall \lambda \in F$  , $\lambda \cdot a = (\lambda a_1,..., \lambda a_n)$
            - Lemma 3.1↔Zero vector is unique
                - Proof through {{ contradiction }}
                    - $0' + x = x$
                    - $0 + x = x$
                    - $0 + 0' = 0' + 0 \implies 0 = 0'$
            - Lemma 3.2 (Cancellation Law)↔Let $V$  be a vector space over $F$ . $\forall x,y,z \in V$ , if $x+z=y+z$ , then $x=y$  
                - corollary↔The additive inverse of any vector is unique
                - proof→Let $x\in V$  and assume there exists $y, y' \in V$  such that $y+x=0$  and $y' + x = 0$ . In particular, $y+x=y'+x$ . Then by the cancellation law, $y=y'$ 
            - Prop 3.1: Let V be a vector space over F ↓ 
                1. $\forall x \in V, 0 \cdot x = 0$
                2. $\forall a \in F, a \cdot 0 = 0$
                3. $\forall a \in F, \forall x  \in V, (-a) \cdot x = a \cdot (-x)$
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/hyVUX0GzxIZjaUU9zSn8cZ8QE2rZ3LAvX2hyhDAL04NVAhOdRGGA-0Z2kiDUS-DbTG1SgpJxFW3ExTsCk5IePwSB5AWGaVil7w_RIOBNkoIXA8Un6cc9R6vy1iQiNCCA.png)
            - Subspace↔A subset $W$  of a vector space $V$  over $F$  is called a subspace if it is a vector space with respect to the operations in $V$ .  In this case we denote $W \leq V$  
                - A subset $W \neq \{\} \subseteq V$  is a subspace $W \leq V$  if and only if
                    - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/Ab_2TdIc9xOuF2NMsh21OE8hEv6xwRGpKI5u9eHyZr7biEAsKHgKJTx6oVvh2Ub9Edk_X1wh0cbJ02-gEUCrLxspIFTE4aFQprhP9fmHxfltT3H4x_m-EiglyRPcZ7h6.png)
                    - Proof: $\implies$  it is implied that operations of $W$  are closed, and so (1) and 2) hold.
$\Longleftarrow$ Assume $W$  satisfies (1) and (2). See rest of notes
                - examples ↓ 
                    - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/YjhjY89ftUtbu9u_c6D0qnh8a4RhxA7qW6qb1_xSukB1k79nUmcmb0qRg0763yXWJVbmKqDecuvPnkWY1-l1Cf9FWn97rcdjOBNFb5EKBZ7gMKFXk5ZEKlpvtAZirzTo.png)
                    - Diagonals
![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/RVELkGR3JvFqNMplvTapf-EakF_m8s30-JoFCfBvp351fUP0RzOhSBZjQ867v2ePaqK3oWo3NA1FckTcp-kQ6BMW_zQRQVnaoxVLZzHaS-gNDbgEyiBXUrUJ3CnhhYr6.png)
                    - a and c are 0

                - Exercise 4.1→In $R^2, U = [\lambda(1,0) | \lambda \in R]$  and $W = [\mu(1,1) | \mu \in R]$ . Prove that $U+W = R^2$ 
![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/TcwTvcyVbBWtvTZwn1zR60RHB7tTTussICmPHSamgUQmjnrnyNfWBiQurNrIldbAqHaSccloghsnSU9kXN0cl8vP4xFbJDMuEBuidMiEOJFOWQ0348-A6a7FDv8ojQ6R.png) 
            - Linear Combinations↔Let $V$  be a vector space over $F$  and let $\subseteq V$  be any subset. We say that an element $v\in V$  is a linear combination of elements of $S$  if there exist a finite number of vectors $u_1,...,u_k\in S$ and scalrs $\alpha _1 , ... , a_k \in F$  such that $v=\alpha_1 u_1 + ... + \alpha_k u_k$ . The set of all linear combinations of elements in $S$  is called the [Spans](Braden Wong/Notes/Yale Courses/Math 230/Day 23: Vector Spaces and Fields & Day 24: Spaces, spans/Spans.md)  of $S$  and denoted $span(S)$

 -- Avoided infinite recursion --     - Lecture 4 Addendum [February 13th, 2021](Daily Document/February 13th, 2021.md)
        - Let $V$  be a vector space over $F$  and let $S$ be any subset. Then $span(S)$  is a subspace containing $S$ . Furthermore, it is the smallest subspace containing $S$  , i.e. for any subspace $U\leq V$  if $S\subseteq U$  then $span(S)\subseteq U$
            - Lemma 4.1↔Given a finite collection of vectors $u_1, ..., u_k \in V$ , any linear combination of these vectors $\alpha_1 u _ 1 + ... + \alpha _ k u_k$ is a vector in $V$ .
            - See notes for more details

        - When can we remove an element from a [Spanning set (aka generating set)](Second Semester/Math 225/Lecture 5 February 19th, 2021/Spanning set (aka generating set).md)  and still be left with a [Spanning set (aka generating set)](Second Semester/Math 225/Lecture 5 February 19th, 2021/Spanning set (aka generating set).md)↔When it's linearly dependent on other vectors #[[Spanning set (aka generating set)]] 
            - $span(u_1,...,u_k)=span(u_1,...,u_k,u_{k+1})$
                - Lets say that $u_{k+1}=u_1+u_2$ . This means that $u_{k+1}$  can be represented by $span(u_1,u_2)$  which is included in $span(u_1+...+u_k)$

            - Braden Wong
                - Notes
                    - Yale Courses
                        - Math 230
                            - Day 25: More vector spaces, subspaces, span, linear independence
                                - Linear independence↔Let $V$  be a vector space over $F$, and $S\subseteq V$. We say $S$ is linearly independent iff $\sum_{i=1}^k c_i\vec s_i = \vec 0$ implies $c_1=c_2=c_3=c_4=...=c_k=0$  . Otherwise, $S$ is linearly independent.
                                    - Properties
                                        - Zero representation↔A linear combination of the form $\sum^k_{i=1}\alpha_iu_i=0$ .
                                        - A set is [Linear independence](Braden Wong/Notes/Yale Courses/Math 230/Day 25: More vector spaces, subspaces, span, linear independence/Linear independence.md)  if all zero-representation by distinct elements are trivial
                                        - If $0\in S$ then $S$  is linearly dependent
                                        - A set containing a linear dependent subset is linear dependent
                                        - A subset of linear independent set is linearly independent

 -- Avoided infinite recursion --         - Basis↔A set $B\subseteq V$  is a basis for $V$  if $B$  is both a [Spanning set (aka generating set)](Second Semester/Math 225/Lecture 5 February 19th, 2021/Spanning set (aka generating set).md) ($span(B)=V)$ and linearly independent
            - It's the minimum viable set needed to construct the vector field
            - Prop 5.1↔Let $V$  be a vector space over $F$  and let $u_1,...,u_n \in V$  be distinct vectors. Then the set $B = [u_1,...,u_n]$  is a basis of $V$  iff every vector $v\in V$  admists exactly one unique representation of the form $V=\sum^n_{1} \beta_iu_i$ , where $\beta$  are uniquely determined by $V$ 
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/7Ylur4AYK2Xd6lQ7nHoDbHoLQvIgwkrWkQJg8mt_yLywS6KvbTKXF1LVbXU8-rmOipVKuq_sqIYnU5bJgW0dBYQUkTp_Iht5hAZFPWDV24GNHFRvHgootvxdbv17N3t1.png) 
            - Every vector space $S$ have a basis
                - Prop 6.1↔Let $V$  be a vector space over $F$  with finite [Spanning set (aka generating set)](Second Semester/Math 225/Lecture 5 February 19th, 2021/Spanning set (aka generating set).md)  $S$ . Then $S$  contains a [Basis](Second Semester/Math 225/Lecture 6 February 19th, 2021/Basis.md)  for $V$ .

        - Finite dimensional↔A vector space $V$  is called finite dimensional whenever it has a finite generating set or basis. The integer $n$  equal to the size of all bases of such $V$  is called its dimension and denoted $n=dim(V)$ . otherwise, a vector space is called infinite dimensional

        - Linear Transformations↔Let $V$  and $W$  be vector spaces over a common field $F$ . A function $T:V\to W$  is called a linear transformation if it satisfies the following two condition
            - $T(x+y)=T(x)+T(y)$ , $\forall x,y \in V$
            - $T(\lambda x) = \lambda \cdot T(x)$ , $\forall x \in V, \lambda \in F$
            - examples→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/64Lp1qXYMwh-MTAfvgclSihQ9s3ixQZsWAHNjrvE4-BSCT--jVOTZUWoZboomU3WAJFRAWQUEsC7tpS95_EAy8ksQU9xykNNu5e7gKmO9xcVTY3lMutYswzDbA6zfZDz.png)

                - Reflections

 -- Avoided infinite recursion --         - Claim 9.1↔All linear transformations $T:R\to R$  are of the form $T(x)=\lambda x$  for some fixed $\lambda \in R$ 
            - proof↔Let $T : R \to R$  be a linear transformation. Then for any $x \in R$ , $T(x) = T(x \cdot 1) = x \cdot T(1) = \lambda x$ .
        - Claim 9.2↔All linear transformations $S: R^2 \to R$  are of the form $S(x,y) = ax+by$ for some fixed $a,b \in R$.
            - Let $S: R^2 \to R$  be a linear transformation, and then for any $(x,y) \in R$, $S(x,y) = S(x\cdot (1,0) + y \cdot (0,1)) = x \cdot S(1,0) + y \cdot S(0,1) = ax + by$ for $a=S((1,0)), b = S((0,1))$ .
        - Proposition 9.1↔Let $V$  and $W$  be two vector spaces over $F$  and assume $dim V = n$ . Let $B= [v_1, ..., v_n]$  be a basis for $V$ . Let $T:V\to W$  be any linear transformation, then $T$  is uniquely determined by the values it gives to $v_1, ...,. v_n$ , that is, $S: V\to W$ is another linear transformation with $S(v_i) = T(v_i)$  then $S=T$ . Moreover, for any choice of vectors $w_1,...,w_n \in W$ there exists a linear transformation $\overline S: V\to W$  with $\overline S (v_i) = w_i$  for all $1\leq i \leq n$ 
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/nWKb6KNozQCzJtS9i02v0hBCJYa-L_aoIB6Arw0kyAERzHXMYByaECz4M-n_jQw9MTds3xSb-yhlJZpC93prAir7OUTN1Hx9Lo8fIbaIeltCqam6JKfoTLrvIx7vT9x6.png)

 -- Avoided infinite recursion --         - [Image of function Im(f)](Braden Wong/Notes/Yale Courses/Math 230/Sets/Image of function Im(f).md)→$Im(f) = \{y \in Y | \exists x \in X f(x) = y\}$  #[[Image of function Im(f)]] 
        - Kernel↔$ker(T) = \{v \in V | T(v) = 0\}$ is the kernel (or null set) of $T$ , given a linear transformation $T: V \to W$  (implicitly assuming $V,W$  are vector spaces over field $F$)
        - Proposition 10.1↔Given a linear transformation $T:V \to W$ , $ker(T)$  is a subspace $V$  and $Im(T)$  is a subspace of $W$ 
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/n1EMQe8U34-ya2iePo56W_y2G-FPtSyFmT_VzUXwQJl72Sq1q4SdNKxTBCcPCGueWIOoeSBPqY761jh7KAtdn5QImusTJz-hS1bfz66jtc5hQJ0uXqwEYPaVBIaX7lOd.png) 
        - Proposition 10.2↔Let $T:V\to W$  be a linear transformation. If $B$  is a basis for $V$ , then $T(B) = \{T(v) | v\in B\}$  is a generating set for $Im(T)$ 
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/G593JzPEGGL8-MGrczsreXA7FVVulvvQ8fRkkGFquxSDuKz1YM1fgyrVD5qPNcHfL3P8rZQtVQ3O77eNKUBImbFp4nDOjVao-7urDWcYl94rYDL0j3GzHHzpu93p1Mhx.png) 
        - Examples of Ker and Im
![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/N7Hu3y6limeGnTHHx-e5VjWWiwyQY6szryrBD_rng99jJiDUAYLeCyvt5Ls_YGi6kO2IBZKB5Vt0HZzp5iL5vov-HhEfvUdaoYFiVw3r_QSthR7Aq0CuzuOkycJaPH-k.png)
        - Proposition 10.3↔Let $T: V\to W$  be a linear transformation. Then $T$  is one-to-one if and only if $ker(T) = [0]$ 
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/Q2bK2O0N-HjB6XnEsWZIhCkbqRU092eYuA3PD2I2X4z7koJhMI2DxiYPchW070IuFWFrNj_23t7MwFSnB0wL24Ud5x47ZstQYSq6n0X1H42zLRhgHThDrTs0ytJIZICj.png) 
        - Dimension theorem↔$dim V = dim(ker(T)) + dim(Im(T))$  for linear transformation $T:V \to W$  given $V,W$  are vector spaces over $F$ 
            - rank of T→$dim(Im(T))$ 
            - nullity of T→$dim(ker(T))$ 
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/ZbxWblpGt7nd7lxGKy_fIVpkh3lPAb3jG8oHMaJOWNKNeqQGmJF44G5EBcv7RiLDhWZh541EzxXkE6S_tTgNxHGXLGtpnnLPIH8aJJ2AU6zqukrFU9vvPchpN0948X_H.png) 
![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/mcgwhFna0ZcwyEFguuivC-rNzlyO7q1HFtSv4h80AuOPRsSEs0pUFDMIXlG3Dxo6-g70jfwvOsgnSgVdXCmGY__8j8YQP0yvueqD01az4p2YHEXzKIBzdA7p3iWbaJXU.png) 
        - Onto↔$T$  is onto $W$  if $Im(T) = W$ 
        - If $dim(ker( T)) = 0$ , then $ker(T) = [0]$
        - Corollary 10.1↔Let $V, W$  be finite-dimensional vector space over $F$ . Assume $dim V = dim W$ . For any linear transformation $T: V\to W$ , $T$  is onto if and only if it's one-to-one
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/1_9pj3pM9t8-qQoqdHONhTpLTOfZSyZxrAJQdwPieIDVp-oEXupNQCIIFZRERIaR0n1IsKFepnydpnZK652inZK-GdRZE4brqWsl_BTtkJHL1_LDDyCnWW9UZ8LTXcNg.png)

        - Matrix representation of linear transformations
            - example→Let $T:R^3\to R^3$  be a linear transformation. Recall that $T$  is uniquely determined by $T(e_1), T(e_2), T(e_3)$. Suppose we denote $T(e_j) = (a_{1j}, a_{2j}, a_{3j})$ for  $j=1,2,3$ . T is uniquely determined by ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/REOm5-ivNT6JVruY6NjsNWtcbpyUNwdREfj67DRdoVUFftapSwtUiCkHEgd3lj3BKFSVyRKiaIvKiWqg6_2DopCJ_xnAD1f8EPppu8t-USbcylJOC1giocYwKkNab5ub.png) and in fact any choice of $a_{ij}$  would correspond to a linear transformation $T:R^3 \to R^3 \implies$  There is a one-to-one correspondence between $T: R^3 \to R^3$  linear transformation $\iff$ $A \in M_3(R)$ 
        - Ordered basis↔Let $V$  be a finite dimensional vector space. An ordered basis of $V$  is a basis of $V$  endowed with a special order
            - example↔In $R^3,$  $\{e_1,e_2,e_3\}$  and $\{e_2, e_1, e_3\}$  are two distinct ordered bases
        - Coordinate of $V$ relative to $B, [V]_B$↔![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/v9aD9BU042UV437QqPHufpzlcw5p8P5hLNmms9rVQgfvNGIiuc5d-rcUD8bhY5Xs-XdF8XWvkXdxaE7UJ0Qvf5p7zdz1CeyE15K8cnfC3BwwHyEvpdbpq03AVkKP8UYD.png) . Note that this is one-to-one onto identification of $V$  with $F^n$ 
            - examples→the following:

        - Invertibility
            - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/LXko5e0vNT-iRH0rigqLVga4cK5HRstG7OHb7vpfvzQjlL7nF-xhiqJ5aa5xVdCNok7EAc7KWnJi0w8Oj-3ZeGZ5OBVd2OK_w5AddxQyubxl700WVs0KXl4FPdlEA6Q0.png)
            - If $g:Y\to Z$ , $f:X \to Y$  are invertible functions, then $g\circ f: X\to Z$  is invertible and $(g\circ f)^{-1}=f^{-1}\circ g^{-1}$ .
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/n6I7i1D1PqgZpimcyFLpb_jdWXeWvkDf7GJVTVr9oWxRjfTcSzkSxOyzaW4xfb3R-3Bv9QIIbnVwcxsBjJvZAJjuigEqcxMRZSSHSFTnCTr81bzlte9DnjwQjVYyyxOx.png)
            - A linear transformation $T:V\to W$  is invertible if it is one-to-one and onto
            - If $T\in L(V,W)$ is invertible then $T^{-1}:W\to V$  is a linear transformation
                - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/D4uy2V5QkFlk-aCF57rWOM1Ye7upFi4VoEwGnnJDZbf2zJGG6ZAnwzaGO9p4LfUSPYBc3ClzHtxQDsZoxNF12_qTEkJaRNWNkRCAbHOlIQQgHUtrNKj2b-JCrdQ3-kFp.png) 
            - Let $T:V\to W$ be invertible linear transformation. Then $V$  is finite dimensional iff $W$ finite dimensional. In such a case, $dim V = dim W$
                - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/gC_mXZiHaT_GmnEDAW-rW3xTz-g6WAVgE7OblXgAo0f_hbTQ1iBo6CRVqTL0sJByBA2Q0o2m7-12QgMzP4kWnwupQhDdRS6WKJlaL4Aucmx3TmY0yeKzqd8u_x4rc_XC.png) 
            - $f: X\to Y$  is invertible iff there exists $g:Y\to X$ s.t. $f\circ g = Id_Y$  and $g\circ f = Id_X$
                - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/Y-jr9RzmZ9mjCHPlUUQFYW_aBZYt4-AeeEcwpi0_-mESlChh6KlwiZnCY9Cof7tCkEW9HcQR0vwQIrS73FCJkVoCjCWdl-1f2rijHxVcbGwBkk_ycvsEWewV81Soh-QL.png) 
        - Matrix invertibility↔$A$  is invertible if there exists $B\in M_n(F)$  satisfying $AB=BA=I_n$ 
            - remark→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/sypqOMOuQmwPAKzVREqipfx9AT4t_F5YfAZpBn-apTVmniX-N2E9g2A92a78UkdLWGD9jv3tzJI31sUMhgAMaz7MiC3G6aVcMgcXrXmmbqZXiKrElqhdMD5LocofZm4L.png) 
            - example→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/2bxWf_AIBi0snML_z17FkvspVlkOIa8IRkRg9_f52ahEV6uyPn_FztPQS-YUyYnLNZBBbXkcHWG8TwPEkjXVRV2CqLKzMYA0EUCpkYC4jAbnqkrT-sYRBxTWcmBcJ9XB.png) 
    - Lecture 15 [March 28th, 2021](Daily Document/March 28th, 2021.md)
        - Recall properties of  linear transformations
            - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/5KCx1zuvdNayQySjZOjXXjspmUE9ZTCBp63mfA65BqRpb00V2H8gs4pLORIkQZ9C89FOOsznmwIYxdIubx-KVPFaSgL0waZjc6j1PbEDJgKt0fxwyK23mL5R2KvtRpIQ.png)
            - examples and antiexamples of invertibility
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/E5ydKZrkQJMEGszNNwCo4prfDX3gwF5fXhoyzB9xL0jp_vPsq0p4VfRda7dlbSPcV0vK91hB_HviWqxCWgwp7iZ9lBdoZSv5EBznShNk5oVy1QFno0OfP4IS8qWRCovt.png)
        - Let $T\in L(V,W)$  with $V,W$  being finite-dimensional vector spaces over $F$  with bases $B$  and $C$ , respectively. Then $T$  is invertible iff $[T]_B^C$ is invertible
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/qXS7VOwvOjlOTXYRAz1jI6WONC2aMTzJuefA4iFV3hTjwAn-ehuUg0dzs_d5Z2bY1C5DAflyMBW5Mo7sfSrqxgzKVm4CJF-z3vPVcsEJTLgLB20SpxT3HXZxFr0pN3Cy.png) 
        - Under the conditions above, $[T^{-1}]_C^B=([T]_C^B)^{-1}$ and $L_A^{-1}=L_{A^{-1}}$ where $L_A\in Ln(F^n)$  with $L_A(x) = Ax$ , whenever $A$  is invertible
            - proof→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/D4ud_440DG9aQdCmLw7ZCJt9g2XEQPsE8EilOZ8qGx6GnJvgWzqXGvB5v95zqK18WyyOlSY4Y7LILrc4MaKKm7I55sbjnkbiEOOvaZzq_NetBdS9AuPPKgNXFbMQ1Dus.png) 
        - Given a matrix $A\in M_{mxn}(F)$ , denote $Ker(A)=[x\in F^n|Ax=0]$
        - Let $A=(a_{ij})\in M_n(F)$ , then the following are equal↔![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/REUiyIcbd6X8mtfp6nrvri0OSZFJCNmCxkkU3KCYhKgGG3U-jAfIYq4HSAbUBWTC4FqmpJ9007pJagbwndhsAM8YPH8P48lzjN_4-cN-cKurgz8Lv5KwRjQeJycV-zsS.png) 
            - example→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/ulcvTw6CorN6LTzLLhDpU_LfzeTlrorq-3DOtFcZLIjicSldW9J5OUUuKbtNgRyqkNgALVk51IzKXy1U6Q0GBghE5NJKEMZVIW0Tw65k9-K_4F4YGEgHKu8UL-OqfiiZ.png) 
        - Isomorphism↔Two vector spaces are said to be isomorphic if there exists an invertible linear transformation between them, called an isomorphism
            - example→![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/j0jJV5FIzMgbdOwuAboYzTJTrU1hRBMNur7GU6Ci2SiMQ9ZzmaLcnX_aIwyGCyOd9H5JeJwGz-g2XF0rDbVwvdg66R_O4kcRkiLAM5NU-pHy6c5gq3vepu-dHVY0z2pu.png) 
        - Change of coordinate matrix

            - From the above
                - $\forall v \in V, [v]_C=[Id_V]_B^C[V]_B$
                - $[Id_V]_B^C$ is invertible with $([Id_V]_B^C)^{-1} = [Id_V]_C^B$

        - Columns span
        - Columns are bases
        - Kernel = 0

            - Normative↔How things should work
            - Positive↔How things do work

    - Lecture 2 [February 4th, 2021](Daily Document/February 4th, 2021.md)
        - First Model
            - Assumptions: One{{ homogenous  }} good, many buyers, many sellers
        - Demand curve is
            - A {{ demand schedule }} listing how much is demanded at each price
            - The {{willingness-to-pay}}  for the {{marginal unit}}
            - Sloping down because of the {{income }}effect and {{substitution}} effect
                - Income effect→can't afford all previous consumption
                - Substitution effect→other goods are relatively more attractive
            - The Law of Demand↔As price increases, quantity demanded decreases (it's not actually a law)
            - Why carbon tasks may be unpopular is because it's a {{ regressive }} tax
        - Inferior vs. normal goods
            - Inferior goods
            - Normal goods
        - Substitutes vs. Complements
            - If price of a good goes up, the demand of **substitute** goes {{up}}
            - If price of good goes up, the demand of **complement** goes {{down}}

    - Lecture 2 [February 3rd, 2021](Daily Document/February 3rd, 2021.md)
        - GDP
            - 3 ways to compute ↓ 
                - GDP as (sum) value added | GDP as final sales
                    - Value added = sales - material input costs
                    - Why not use GDP as final sales rather than sum of value added?→Because it's difficult to distinguish the final sales and the intermediate sales. We want to count only value added
                - GDP as Gross Domestic Income (Total income of everyone in an economy)
                    - GDP = payments of {{labor}} and {{capital}}
                        - Payments of capital→Rental expenditures and profits
                        - In income, but not GDP→Capital gains and net foreign Income
                        - In GDP, but not income→Depreciation
                - GDP as Gross Domestic Expenditure
                    - Y = C + I + G + NX
                        - C→Consumption
                        - I→Investment (Purchase of capital, housing construction, inventories)
                            - Inventories
                            - Unsold output goes into inventory and is counted as {{ inventory investment }}
                                - Assumption is that firms purchase their {{unsold output}}
                        - G→Government
                            - Purchase of goods and services (does not include transfer like social security and unemployment to avoid {{double-counting}} in consumption)
                        - NX→Net Exports (Export - import)
                - Note: The rent of a house, both actual and {{would-be}} cost is included
            - Measure GDP of government as {{ value added }} evaluated at their cost
            - Measuring [GDP](Second Semester/Econ 116/Lecture 2 February 3rd, 2021/GDP.md)  through different methods
                - Example 1: [GDP as (sum) value added | GDP as final sales](Second Semester/Econ 116/Lecture 2 February 3rd, 2021/GDP/3 ways to compute/GDP as (sum) value added | GDP as final sales.md)![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/6UHasnUhYYqmkNX9qX4cjQDTcGxf0kULSGVBGjOJE44JfucRn5hGA7JH6nGepFK1ZDCIfmxpsiIifHy4h4D-UAq8FAEjrPl_N0R_SunYSy9npLOxrB59yRVZuD2NI75r.png)
                    - value added and GDP→100 + 75 + 125 ⇒ 300
                - Example 2:  [GDP as (sum) value added | GDP as final sales](Second Semester/Econ 116/Lecture 2 February 3rd, 2021/GDP/3 ways to compute/GDP as (sum) value added | GDP as final sales.md)![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/vhZxO2-ueRLpGnyLRrX8dh0oXsEgHFaxl9zxfTOQ0CSN03p0EB8Wc9M_K0KnwnrrTJebqdBt3mwg2ATvtDDJhBF3moBMZiZGAwi-Ukgwk5ZAMF4XDU3MxYYlcZ66ETXp.png)
                - Example 3: [Measure GDP of government as  value added  evaluated at their cost](Second Semester/Econ 116/Lecture 2 February 3rd, 2021/GDP/Measure GDP of government as  value added  evaluated at their cost.md)![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/4JKw-roW-sabUZcYPdZEPi1U0zJHctLpj7QDtPFCTrE1kopwoVOraaDhpkm85lAlB9jX09GK75UVaNnnPuxnrfro8coCAe2ZVrHE_5540wxIdN6h6qEyQwbY-RUiJISS.png)
                - Example 4: ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/gltDwyD7FyZmlJF031I_ZKJK8RqTtNe3eN8z6wKCFeDCQZNQFn6ue3Ci5wyMyWgOerzCnGQSfM-xyXtAv9JpBBj_tPRcPNUc_XjR4maEHEbnMcf_OuKeAJnZDbuXB3gf.png)
                - Example 5: Using all of the different methods![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/Mpyc9qxdiZprvX-YiPgzvgTDOY9U5LfVuE1O62spj_YRMjMrGLqpUfoS6Y_9XLDv6sgMOfp2pJrglWXM8Z9_4TF3AiGk1L7-lbGk_b-dKqTjFI4MzF5Nz_gE1CMLzVcM.png)
        - Nominal vs. Real GDP
            - Nominal GDP→GDP using current prices
            - Real GDP→GDP using baseline price (price of goods at a certain yer)
            - GDP deflator =→$\frac{Nominal GDP}{Real GDP}$ 
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/NlqVAPiZrwDai50I_n9TgSgnsG5qxuNCDbSOKvsdv-HDlZyvqQDncbej-Rjcgeq-GDO6KolB5Uj08P-3OJxt04JHm5ZfOVwccZrHsRTJxcRrMGx_fz543oI7tKWfZQWk.png)
        - Alternative metric, Jones and Klenow
            - Assume you have an equal  chance of being born in a country
            - Add GDP, Leisure, Welfare, Life Expectancy
        - GDP Issues
            - High GDP but high savings (like China) = low saving
            - High GDP but low leisure (like the US)

            - He was placed behind a glass box to prevent assassination
            - The death penalty was resurrected

            - Lack of evidence: There was only a shred such as "Eichmann proposes shooting"
            - Psychologists examined that he was totally normal
            - “I will jump into my grave laughing, because the fact that I have the death of five million Jews [or “enemies of the Reich,” as he always claimed to have said]on my conscience gives me extraordinary satisfaction.”

    - Lecture 4 [February 11th, 2021](Daily Document/February 11th, 2021.md)
        - Jeremy Bentham, “Introduction to the Principles of Morals and Legislation,” Chs. 1-3, 7 P
            - A useful extremist of **classical utilitarianism**
            - The principle of utility
            - Vain to talk of the interest of the community without understanding interest of individual
            - Features ↓ 
                1. Comprehensive and deterministic ↓ 
                    1. comprehensiveNothing it cannot explain ↓ 
                        1. Objection: What if I do things for religious motivation? You follow religious motivation by pleasure
                    2. deterministic↔Predicts everything
                2. Naturalistic→We are bound to the principle of utility by "the natural constitution of the human frame". **Physical** source of pain is the fundamental drive for our behavior, and **physical** pain and pleasure drives u 
                3. Egoistic, but not subjectivist ↓ 
                    - Concerning oneself, self-interest
                    - Objectivist view. You might not know why you do something, but scientists can distill your desires to a fundamental truth
                4. Consequentialism↔Only cares about outcome—not moral sense, natural law, rule of right
                5. Quantifiable↔by intensity, duration, certainty/uncertainty, remoteness (discount rate)
            - The question is not can they reason, but can they suffer?
            - Bentham considered animal suffering, which was ahead of his time
            - Karl Popper vs. R.N. Smart↔Utilitarianism cannot just be about minimizing suffering
                - benevolent explosion↔Smart's critique that if there was a painless way to kill all humans, then according to Popper, we should do it
            - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/InjOLOKrmiZKCoF7uHY0BVzkkAqmo3jxPgU-oZt_F1-pb2pSlGNO7jz-KXXaVokNsOaTnmnbRrR7wNJ0GiDDWnE2oWfhg0JdeCg8oaU6jR_3a8CWNSHxuO0_P7nPozlf.png)
            - Bentham believed that you can make{{ interpersonal comparisons of }}utility
            - Objections to Bentham
                - [The experience machine](Braden Wong/Notes/Yale Courses/First Semester/Life/Week 1/The experience machine.md)→Also known as a happiness machine, dreamed up by Nozick  #[[The experience machine]]  #[[The experience machine]] 
                - Utility monster↔Someone experiences way more happiness than someone else

            - Is / Ought problem↔Is does not imply ought
                - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/V9w1JCOl4ydqFFMOeE6yNWtU48p9PakI9j8ZPSTtvohncYpDoNvp4GKRkCUW3bRhlOd-aEkM5E5ByE-NxQh3L1xgZTRViIipwXR6P0rKQ5FmJ8dSJ1eIg1LSWeaOotg-.png)
        - Ayer's Logical Positivism
            - Three kinds of assertions
                - Analytical truths
                - Empirical truths
                - Everything else = meaningless nonsense
        - Logical positivism versus legal positivism
            - Bentham argued there is no natural law
                - Entirely hinging on utilitarianism
                - Why Bentham argues that we should we have rights↔Practical equality. We want rights for consequentialist reasons
                - There is a degree of workmanship. So the government has a responsibility to protect those who craft value, its citizens
            - Bentham's radical ideas↔He advocated individual and economic freedom, the separation of church and state, freedom of expression, equal rights for women, the right to divorce, and the decriminalising of homosexual acts. [My note: he lived from 1747-1832, well before most of these views were common.] He called for the abolition of slavery, the abolition of the death penalty, and the abolition of physical punishment, including that of children. He has also become known in recent years as an early advocate of animal rights.
            - Evaluate scientific (legal positivism)
            - ![](https://remnote-user-data.s3.amazonaws.com/SEyczd9jOoq4b2A5GYcRVd78MK8eqTIQ3tNJopqrKJDG5tZ9-wpx9UIITC5jqusLAo4S_sG2Z7CxOG71qoJuqAY5VEfkC-ClUu1lCHbZekacjY7d7tGDjmS5m6FAWfxo.png)
            - Emotivism↔Ethical and moral arguments simply describe your moral state/how you feel rather than what is
            - Cost him his job at Yale, it was crazy

    - Lecture 5 [February 23rd, 2021](Daily Document/February 23rd, 2021.md)
        - John Stuart Mill
            - On Liberty, Ch. 1-2
                - On the limiting of powers
                    - The struggle between Liberty and Authority is the most conspicuous feature in the portions of history with which we are earliest familiar, particularly in that of Greece, Rome, and England. But in old times this contest was between subjects, or some classes of subjects, and the government. By liberty, was meant protection against the tyranny of the political rulers. The rulers were conceived (except in some of the popular governments of Greece) as in a necessarily antagonistic position to the people whom they ruled. They consisted of a governing One, or a governing tribe or caste, who derived their authority from inheritance or conquest, who, at all events, did not hold it at the pleasure of the governed, and whose supremacy men did not venture, perhaps did not desire, to contest, whatever precautions might be taken against its oppressive exercise. Their power was regarded as necessary, but also as highly dangerous; as a weapon which they would attempt to use against their subjects, no less than against external enemies. To prevent the weaker members of the community from being preyed upon by innumerable vultures, it was needful that there should be an animal of prey stronger than the rest, commissioned to keep them down. But as the king of the vultures would be no less bent upon preying on the flock than any of the minor harpies, it was indispensable to be in a perpetual attitude of defence against his beak and claws. The aim, therefore, of patriots, was to set limits to the power which the ruler should be suffered to exercise over the community; and this limitation was what they meant by liberty. It was attempted in two ways. First, by obtaining a recognition of certain immunities, called political liberties or rights, which it was to be regarded as a breach of duty in the ruler to infringe, and which if he did infringe, specific resistance, or general rebellion, was held to be justifiable. A second, and generally a later expedient, was the establishment of constitutional checks; by which the consent of the community, or of a body of some sort, supposed to represent its interests, was made a necessary condition to some of the more important acts of the governing power. To the first of these modes of limitation, the ruling power, in most European countries, was compelled, more or less, to submit. It was not so with the second; and to attain this, or when already in some degree possessed, to attain it more completely, became everywhere the principal object of the lovers of liberty. And so long as mankind were content to combat one enemy by another, and to be ruled by a master, on condition of being guaranteed more or less efficaciously against his tyranny, they did not carry their aspirations beyond this point
                - On the liberty of thought and discussion
                    - The best government has no more title to it than the worst. It is as noxious, or more noxious, when exerted in accordance with public opinion, than when in or opposition to it. If all mankind minus one, were of one opinion, and only one person were of the contrary opinion, mankind would be no more justified in silencing that one person, than he, if he had the power, would be justified in silencing mankind
            - Held father in contempt for raising him on utilitarian principles
                - Taught with tutors to max utility
                - Fluent in Greek and Latin, brilliant mathematician
                - But had no friends
            - On Liberty was written with careful consultation with his wife
